<Pics>None</Pics>< Review>
Would have been 5 star but only 3 other groups (1, 2 and 2 in each) and dining room had zero clean tables, grabbed handful of napkins and water from bathroom sink and cleaned one for us to use. There was a few cars in the drive through but had an employee dedicated for that. 2 people in kitchen area and 2 manning the counter...surely someone could give the dining room a quick wipe down. The cabinets were full of chicken, so they were not swamped. But food was great...hot fresh and tasted fantastic. Live less than 1.5
miles away and go here often; but usually drive through and often they are out of chicken (around 2 hours before closing) we will then drive to the Santa Rosa location and get chicken there. 14 mile round trip seems silly when there is this location so much closer...but when you want chicken, you want chicken!</Review>

The team at Allied has always been prompt in responding, provide fair prices for their work, and we've never had any issues with work they've done on our cars. <Review>I had an odd experience here. They gave me a $188 oil change with a $100 labor charge without providing an estimate first. California's Automotive Repair Act says an estimate must be provided first.
They wanted to charge me over $700 to reseal valve covers, about double what most shops would charge -- and it wasn't necessary, according to the second opinion that I got. As a tie breaker, I parked my car over some paper: no sign of a leak.
This shop very thoroughly checked my car for problems, finding several other issues including a brake light that needed to be replaced, yet they did not even mention that my check engine light was on.
This is probably a great shop to use if you have a nice car and lots of money to spend. I do not; the total cost of the suggested repairs was double the blue book value of my car.< /Review><user_id>104328412811779134329< /user_id>< Name>

< review>
My family was on our way to the mountains when my truck blew a coolant hose at the gas station. I quickly googled the closest auto shop and Allied Autoworks was right around the corner. My truck is a diesel and so I figured it was a shot in the dark that they would be able to help but I drove over anyways. The staff was incredibly friendly and sympathetic to my situation and immediately dove in to take a look. They located the leak and did a little research to figure out the size of a tiny hose that had developed a pin hole. Even with the shop packed with vehicles, they saw that I was in distress having two young children with me and they prioritized the repair getting me in and out in an hours time. My family and I were able to reliably continue our drive and have a great weekend. I love businesses with extremely great customer service and Allied Autoworks gives the best customer service I‚Äôve seen. I cannot recommend this place enough. Give your business to people who care about you and your needs. Take your vehicle to Allied.</review>

< review>
The building is great. It was an old post office. Wood work inside is beautiful. Along with 4 safes built into the walls. The most amazing thing to me was. In the 70's the building was moved 150 yards to it's location today. It was the only building saved and moved. So the Santa Rosa Mall could be built. Post offices are built like banks or bomb shelters. So I'm sure it was no easy task.
Three stars because it cost $10 to enter. It's more of a art museum not so much on history. But for that $10. It will get you in their next door building. The actual art museum. Both buildings are rather empty. Both don't need to be art. Show some history.<//review>

<Text>BEYOND BOLLYWOOD- Exhibit at the Sonoma County Museum,Santa Rosa, California. Speechless was I for a long time after I left the museum. What an amazing capsule of the history of Indian Immigrants and their contribution to the American Scene, a treasure indeed did I see. For Indophiles and especially for East Indians both young and old this a must. For here one can walk through time itself, from way past to the present. Pictures reflecting personal histories, so touching, covered a wide range of professions. The descriptions were brief yet succinct. Smithsonian curator, Dr. Masum Momaya has done an incredibly creative and attractive presentation that is bound to make Indian Americans who live here, both humble and proud at the same time. Museum Curator, Eric Stanley , Volunteer Coordinator Cynthia Leung and staff have enhanced the Smithsonian exhibits with entries in the form of displays and educational presentations of local origin. Exhibit will be there until Jan 10 2016.< /Text>< Pics>

<user_id>101997587807451112154< /user_id>< username>
Angela G.<//username>
< time>
1499485517378< /time>
<rating>5</rating><review>This charming history museum is far superior to most small city history museums, both in scope and in presentation.  Most history museums are static.  Once you've been there you never need to go again.  Most tell the story (however well they tell it varies widely) of a particular town or city, often chronologically, hitting the highlights...and that's it.  Not Sonoma County History Museum.  This museum covers a wide cultural scope, including the entirety of Sonoma County.  The shows and exhibits change 3 or 4 times a year, so there is always a reason to go back, and then back again.  Sonoma County has a rich history, from pre-European times to present day.  Eric Stanley, the museum's curator and major driving force, is not just knowledgeable, but creative, and presents each show with verve and a deft hand.

The present show, which ends July 9,  explores  "the Great War" at it's 100th anniversary, with a boffo major private collection of iconic WWI posters, plus some artifacts and letters from Sonoma County to cement the local connection.  The museum also includes lectures on various show topics, including, for the current show, the tragic story of the Spanish Flu, which overlapped with and was partially spread by soldiers in WWI.

Past shows have included the story of Russians who long ago settled Sonoma County's coast; the history and legacy of Chinese immigrants;  a  the history of the bicycle;  a touching and surprising show about Santa Rosa's Korean sister city, Jeju; an exhibit last year about guitars through the ages, called Medieval to Metal, showcasing fabulous instruments owned by famous musicians you know and loved.

The next upcoming show is about the history of the horse in Sonoma County.  Based on the shows that have come before, I'll be first in line for this one.  AND there is a bonus.  If you buy a ticket to a show at the History Museum (in a lovely 1910 building, formerly a Post Office), you also get admission to the new Sonoma County Museum of Art, which is right next door.  Plus there is a cool sculpture garden to tour.  What a deal!  What a treasure for Santa Rosa and Sonoma County.< /review><pictures>None</pictures><Resp>None< /Resp>< gmapID>

< Review>
Our air conditioner was in desperate need of repair last summer, but we weren't quite in the market to purchase a new unit. Mike Brady, the owner of Lucky Air came out promptly on a Sunday, during one of the hottest days of the year. He replaced/repaired a few items to get our family through the blazing heat and helped hold our household over until we were ready to purchase a replacement unit.

After months of extensive research and many informative emails and phone calls back and forth to Mike, we decided on the Lennox XC-25 Air Conditioner. We also purchased a SLP98V furnace to replace our outdated one.

I can't say enough great things about both units. They are so quiet compared to the old ones! The variable level cooling of the XC-25 ensures that every room is cooled to perfection. I was really excited about the ability to control the unit through my cell phone too; such an incredibly convenient feature that was much easier to use than I had initially anticipated. I can't wait to compare my energy bills this summer!

The installation duo from Lucky Air were very professional and personable; they arrived promptly and finished the job in a timely manner. I was especially impressed with the condition in which they left the area, everything was very tidy, no loose ends! I was pleasantly surprised when I received an unexpected follow up call from Mike a few days after the install. This team knows their trade and they manage to accomplish their work with a level of honesty and integrity rarely seen these days.

Bravo to the group of professionals at Lucky Air, my hat is tipped to you. My family and I thank you for keeping us comfortable. I'll definitely recommend this company to my family and friends.< /Review>

The beach is fantastic during low tide. It is notorious for containing multiple tide pools, as well as rocky beaches and rocks to climb. Wildlife as always is present, and you can get some fantastic pictures here. Parking and restrooms are, not a problem in this area, as they're both nearby. This is a fantastic place for pictures, as it provides interesting rock formations. If you can, climb up the big rock that's located on the north-western point of the beach, and you will get some fantastic shots of the scenery. Coming here during high-tide is not advised, as none of the things mentioned above are accessible due to the high water level. All in all, a great place to come especially if you're in the area.< /Review>< resp>

I was visited this beach on July/10/20.
It is small beach but it is perfect for all ages.
It has everything I‚Äôm looking for.
There is no parking fee, and street parking too.
It has a basic bathroom, no sink, but its clean when I was there.
It is breathtaking and fun place.
All little and big rocks come with different colors and shapes, they are very pretty.
If you like to collect rocks, this is the beach for you to find your favor.
It has few little caves, interesting rock formations, cliffs for me to hop back and forth very fun, and a huge adventure rock to climb up to enjoy the view of the Pacific Ocean.
I definitely will come back here again.< /text>
